123164 LVINLBVWe
123182 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
123497 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
123897 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
124081 GPIB status vector:
124102 status[0] - Device Clear State
124133  status[1] - Device Trigger State
124167  status[2] - Listener Active State
124203 status[3] - Talker Active State
124236 status[4] - Attention line asserted
124273 status[5] -
124285 Controller In Charge
124306  status[6] - Remote State
124332  status[7] - Lockout State
124360 status[8] - I/O Completed 
124388 status[9] - not used
124409  status[10]- not used
124431  status[11]- not used
124454 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
124494 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
124526  status[14]- Timeout occured
124555  status[15]- GPIB error detected
124591 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
124644 GPIB Error:
124661 -No error
124676 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
124715 -No listeners detected on write
124752 -Controller not addressed correctly
124793 -Invalid argument(s)
124820 (perhaps bad address string????)
124858 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
124896 -I/O operation aborted
124924 -hardware not present
124951 -DMA error
124967 -DMA bus timeout
124989 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
125028 progress
125042 -function not implemented
125073 -file system error
125097 -shareable board exclusively owned
125137 -GPIB bus error (commands)
125169 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
125197 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
125230 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
125320 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
125654 GPIB status vector:
125675 status[0] - Device Clear State
125706  status[1] - Device Trigger State
125740  status[2] - Listener Active State
125776 status[3] - Talker Active State
125809 status[4] - Attention line asserted
125846 status[5] -
125858 Controller In Charge

125905  status[7] - Lockout State
125933 status[8] - I/O Completed 
125961 status[9] - not used
125982  status[10]- not used
126004  status[11]- not used
126027 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
126067 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
126099  status[14]- Timeout occured
126128  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

182659 -No error

183228 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
183320 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
183504 GPIB status vector:
183525 status[0] - Device Clear State
183556  status[1] - Device Trigger State
183590  status[2] - Listener Active State
183626 status[3] - Talker Active State
183659 status[4] - Attention line asserted
183696 status[5] -
183708 Controller In Charge
183729  status[6] - Remote State
183755  status[7] - Lockout State
183783 status[8] - I/O Completed 
183811 status[9] - not used
183832  status[10]- not used
183854  status[11]- not used
183877 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
183917 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
183949  status[14]- Timeout occured
183978  status[15]- GPIB error detected
184012 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
184265 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
184575 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
184688   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
184736  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
184783  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device.

331697 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
331955      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
332006      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.

332111      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
332168      error, and a positive value is a warning.

437749 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
438057 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
438333 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
438678 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

634319 LVINLBVW
634339 (I32) 
634346 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
634598 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
634943      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
634995      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
635053      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
635110      error, and a positive value is a warning.
635158      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
635208      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
635257 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

635420 ERROR
635427 (ABC) 
635434 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
635617 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
635875      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
635926      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
635973      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
636031      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
636088      error, and a positive value is a warning.
636136      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
636183      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
636232 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

744138 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
744483      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
744535      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
744593      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
744650      error, and a positive value is a warning.
744698      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
744748      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
744797 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
744937 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
745167 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
745214 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
745245 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
745303 Optional Parameter Default Values:
745338     bd - GPIB board (0)
745362     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
745403     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
745448     logical addr - VXI logical address 
745489 EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
745587 INSTR{GPIB::5}"
745604 no error
745613 ERROR
745619 no error
745628 ERROR
745635 (ABC) 
745642 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
745825 (I32) 
745832 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
746083 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
746341      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
746392      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
746439      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
746497      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
746554      error, and a positive value is a warning.
746602      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
746649      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
746698 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

746813 ERROR
746820 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
747060 (i32) The error code associated with an error.  Possible values:
747126 0  Success
747137 -1200  Invalid syntax string
747166 -1201  Error finding instruments
747199 -1202  Unable to initialize interface or instrument
747251 -1205  Invalid instr handle

872358 &Opens an existing file, creates a new file, or replaces an existing file, programmatically or interactively using dialog.  You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern, and you can specify open and deny modes when opening a file, plus group and permission when creating a new file. Use this VI with the intermediate Write File+ or Read File+ VIs described below.
872772 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
872992 function is the operation to perform:
873032 0 (open) opens an existing file.  Error 7 occurs if the file cannot be found.
873113 1 (open or create) opens an existing file or creates a new file if one does not exist.
873202 2 (create or replace) creates a new file or replaces a file if it exists and you give permission.  Replacement is done by opening the file and setting EOF to 0.  Error 43 occurs if the user elects to disallow the replacement using dialog.  
873445 3 (create) creates a new file.  Error 8 occurs if the file already exists.
873521 advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if function=0 and the file does not exist, or if function=2 or 3 and the file exists.
873666 prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
873762 default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
873855 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
874037 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
874207 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
874741 new file path is the path of the file opened or created.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open or create using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
874976 refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
875083 file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
875172 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern, and you can specify open and deny modes when opening a file, plus group and permission when creating a new file. Use this VI with the intermediate Write File+ or Read File+ VIs described below.
925991 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
926211 function is the operation to perform:
926251 0 (open) opens an existing file.  Error 7 occurs if the file cannot be found.
926332 1 (open or create) opens an existing file or creates a new file if one does not exist.
926421 2 (create or replace) creates a new file or replaces a file if it exists and you give permission.  Replacement is done by opening the file and setting EOF to 0.  Error 43 occurs if the user elects to disallow the replacement using dialog.  
926664 3 (create) creates a new file.  Error 8 occurs if the file already exists.
926740 advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if function=0 and the file does not exist, or if function=2 or 3 and the file exists.
926885 prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
926981 default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
927074 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
927256 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
927426 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
927960 new file path is the path of the file opened or created.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open or create using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
928195 refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
928302 file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
928391 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

942817 lprompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories (or folders) in the file dialog.
942978 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory (or folder) in a file dialog. The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory (or folder) shown in a file dialog.
943206 \default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
943425 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories (or folders). See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
943619 =!L#X
943650 new file path is the path of the file opened or created. You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open or create using dialog. new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
943886 Astatus is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.
944093 *error in is a cluster of three elements (status, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existence of any error proceeding the execution of the VI. The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.
944396 vsource is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
944532 0code is the error code; the default value is 0.
944680 c<'[
944707 file path is the path name of the file. If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file. Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.
944922 irefnum is the reference number of the open file. The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
945032 %status is TRUE if an error occurred.
945093 function is the operation to perform:
945135 opens an existing file. Error 7 occurs if the file cannot be found.
945207 opens an existing file or creates a new file if one does not exist.
945279 creates a new file or replaces a file if it exists and you give permission. Replacement is done by opening the file and setting EOF to 0. Error 43 occurs if the user elects to disallow the replacement using dialog. 
945499 creates a new file. Error 8 occurs if the file already exists.
945614 code is the error code.
945642 Psource is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
945729 )error out is a cluster of three elements (status, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI. If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
946093 Xfile size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
946187 advisory dialog? Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if function=0 and the file does not exist, or if function=2 or 3 and the file exists.

984609 Open/Create/Replace File.vi
990055 *Writes a string of characters to a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the end of file.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not write if an incoming error occurs.
990278 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
990328 pos mode specifies where the write begins relative to pos offset:
990399 at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
990450 at the end of the file plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
990523 at the current file mark plus pos offset.
990566 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
990702 character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
990759 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert the LabVIEW end of line marker to the platform-specific marker.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
990899 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
991433 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
991503 mark after write is the location of the character following the last character written.
991592 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
991899 MThis verison of Serial Port Reset.vi is for the Windows 3 version of LabVIEW.
991988 This version of Set Serial Port Buffer Size.vi is to be used on the SPARC or Windows version of LabVIEW as a subVI to OpenSerialDriver and Serial Port Init.vi.
994928 Measure volts, amps, or ohms.  Select one of 6 functions.  Select range or use auto range.  Select trigger mode.  Slow reading rate is used for accuracy.                                         version a.0
995672 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
995967 VFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
996073 This VI writes the value in pattern to the port identified by task ID.
996145 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
996319 ZFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
996425 This VI reads the port identified by task ID and returns the pattern read.
996501 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
996676 For most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
996781 This VI establishes a port configuration. You can use the task ID that this VI returns only in digital port VIs.
996895 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
997199 aCompares 2 real numbers X and Y.  If they are within about 0.1% of each other a TRUE is returned.
997439 @Initializes the selected serial port to the specified settings.
997511 QWrites the data in string to write to the serial port indicated in port number. 
997603 qReads the number of characters specified by requested byte count from the serial port indicated in port number. 
997727 kReturns in byte count the number of bytes in the input buffer of the serial port indicated in port number.
997844 This vi performs general purpose RS-232 communication.
997899 Timeout: (value in seconds)
997927 Mode:
997933 0 = write then read, 1 = write only, 2 = read only
997984 Port Select:
997997 0 = com1, 1 = com2
998024 This vi handles the RS-232 communications for a UUT. FC In and FC Out are used for flow control.
998121 Mode 0 - Write then Read.
998147 Mode 1 - Write only.
998168 Mode 2 - Read only.
998188 Timeout is in seconds.
998219 GOpens an existing file programmatically or interactively using dialog.  You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern.   Error 7 occurs if the file does not exist.  Use this VI with the intermediate level Read File+ VIs described below.
998505 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
998725 advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if the file does not exist.
998812 prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
998908 default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
999001 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
999183 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
999353 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
999887 new file path is the path of the file opened.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
1000101 refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
1000208 file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
1000297 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
1000604 This subVI tests the error status output of one or more low-level functions or subVIs that output a numeric error code, and creates an error out cluster that can be wired to the Simple or General Error Handler in order to identify the error and describe it to the user.
1000875 The error in cluster is tested first.  If error? is no-error, the elements of the error codes array are tested next for non-zero values.  The first error found terminates the test, and error out identifies that error.  Use a Build Array function to assemble the individual error codes.
1001162 You can optionally use the source messages string to pass on the source of the error. Enter one line of text for each element of the error codes array.  
1001317 The error? status  is TRUE on any error.
1001367 QCloses the file on command or when in incoming error occurs and returns the file size at closure.
1001467 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1001517 close when?  Set TRUE (default) when you want to close the file when this VI is called.  Set to FALSE when you want to close the file only if this VI encounters an incoming error.  This input is useful when you use this VI inside a loop and want to close the file only on the last loop iteration or on an upstream error.  In that case, set close when? TRUE on the last iteration, and terminate the loop on the last iteration or when this VI returns an error. 
1001978 file size is the size of the file in bytes at the time the file is closed; the value is zero otherwise.
1002083 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1002617 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1002687 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
1002996 Reads a string of characters from a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the current mark.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not read if an incoming error occurs.
1003219 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1003269 pos mode specifies where the reads begins relative to pos offset:
1003340 at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
1003391 at the end of the file plus pos offset.
1003436 at the current file mark plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
1003507 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
1003643 count is the number of bytes to read.
1003682 line mode  Set TRUE to read until a line marker or end of line is encounter or count characters are read.  Set FALSE (default value) to read until count characters are read or end of line is encountered.  A line mark is a carriage return, a line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed.
1003981 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert each platform-specific end of line marker to the LabVIEW marker, line feed.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
1004133 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1004667 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1004737 character string is the data read from the file.
1004787 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
1004927 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
1005235 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
1005808 Writes a character string to a new byte stream file or appends the string to an existing file.  The VI opens or creates the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.
1005975 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1006195 character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
1006252 append to file?  Set to TRUE if you want to append the data to a existing file; you can also set it TRUE to write to a new file.  Set to FALSE (default value) if you want to write the data to a new file or to replace an existing file.
1006488 new file path is the path of the file to which the VI wrote data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
1006732 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1006911 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
1007002 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
1007236 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
1007372 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.
1007508 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1007687 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
1007815 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
1008038 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
1008173 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.
1008307 5Generalized DIO96 control.
1008336 Device:  Card ID.
1008354 Port Number: (0-11); APA=0, APB=1,APC=2,BPA=3,...
1008404 Port Width: Width of port in # of bits.
1008444 Initialize: If zero, port will be initialized.
1008491 Input: Data, if any, to be written to the port.
1008539 Read/Write: Bool., F=Read, T=Write.
1008575 Output: Data written to or read from port.
1008628 --------------LOAD SELECT--------------------------------------
1008692 DEFAULT:
1008701     0=1.1MOhm connected to UUT leads; Same as '9'.
1008752 LOW Voltage side:
1008770     1=100k; 2=10k; 3=1k; 4=100; 5=10; 6=2k;
1008814     7=0%(DA); 8=10% (DA)
1008839 HIGH Voltage side:
1008858     9=100k 
1008870 ______________________________________
1008909 Settling Time:  Delay(mS) for relays to settle.
1008957                        Default: 200mS
1008995 ______________________________________
1009034 FC In/Out:  Flow control terminals
1009075 *Reads a specified number of lines from a byte stream file beginning at a specified character offset.  The VI opens the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.
1009238 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1009458 number of lines is the maximum number of lines the VI reads.  The default value is -1 line, which means to read the entire file.  For this VI, a line is a character string ending with a carriage return, line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed; a string ending at the EOF; or a string that has the maximum line length specified by the max characters per line input.
1009840 start of read offset is the position in the file, measured in characters (or bytes), at which the VI begins reading.
1009958 max characters per line is the maximum number of characters the VI reads before ending the search for the end of a line.  The default is 0, which means that there is no limit to the number of characters the VI reads.
1010176 new file path is the path of the file from which the VI read data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
1010411 line string is the data read from the file.
1010456 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
1010596 EOF? is TRUE if you attempt to read past the end of file.

1044965 compatWriteText.vi
1045059 *Writes a string of characters to a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the end of file.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not write if an incoming error occurs.
1045282 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1045332 pos mode specifies where the write begins relative to pos offset:
1045403 at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
1045454 at the end of the file plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
1045527 at the current file mark plus pos offset.
1045570 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
1045706 character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
1045763 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert the LabVIEW end of line marker to the platform-specific marker.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
1045903 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1046437 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1046507 mark after write is the location of the character following the last character written.
1046596 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1700899 V&*?
1701043 GOpens an existing file programmatically or interactively using dialog.  You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern.   Error 7 occurs if the file does not exist.  Use this VI with the intermediate level Read File+ VIs described below.
1701329 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1701549 advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if the file does not exist.
1701636 prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
1701732 default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
1701825 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
1702007 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
1702177 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1702711 new file path is the path of the file opened.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
1702925 refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
1703032 file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
1703121 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1719100 This subVI tests the error status output of one or more low-level functions or subVIs that output a numeric error code, and creates an error out cluster that can be wired to the Simple or General Error Handler in order to identify the error and describe it to the user.
1719371 The error in cluster is tested first.  If error? is no-error, the elements of the error codes array are tested next for non-zero values.  The first error found terminates the test, and error out identifies that error.  Use a Build Array function to assemble the individual error codes.
1719658 You can optionally use the source messages string to pass on the source of the error. Enter one line of text for each element of the error codes array.  
1719813 The error? status  is TRUE on any error.

1730337 Find First Error.vi
1730427 QCloses the file on command or when in incoming error occurs and returns the file size at closure.
1730527 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1730577 close when?  Set TRUE (default) when you want to close the file when this VI is called.  Set to FALSE when you want to close the file only if this VI encounters an incoming error.  This input is useful when you use this VI inside a loop and want to close the file only on the last loop iteration or on an upstream error.  In that case, set close when? TRUE on the last iteration, and terminate the loop on the last iteration or when this VI returns an error. 
1731038 file size is the size of the file in bytes at the time the file is closed; the value is zero otherwise.
1731143 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1731677 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1731747 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1743061 compatReadText.vi
1743160 Reads a string of characters from a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the current mark.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not read if an incoming error occurs.
1743383 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1743433 pos mode specifies where the reads begins relative to pos offset:
1743504 at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
1743555 at the end of the file plus pos offset.
1743600 at the current file mark plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
1743671 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
1743807 count is the number of bytes to read.
1743846 line mode  Set TRUE to read until a line marker or end of line is encounter or count characters are read.  Set FALSE (default value) to read until count characters are read or end of line is encountered.  A line mark is a carriage return, a line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed.
1744145 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert each platform-specific end of line marker to the LabVIEW marker, line feed.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
1744297 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1744831 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1744901 character string is the data read from the file.
1744951 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
1745091 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1777703 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

1797465 Close File+.vi
1797552 Writes a character string to a new byte stream file or appends the string to an existing file.  The VI opens or creates the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.
1797719 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1797939 character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
1797996 append to file?  Set to TRUE if you want to append the data to a existing file; you can also set it TRUE to write to a new file.  Set to FALSE (default value) if you want to write the data to a new file or to replace an existing file.
1798232 new file path is the path of the file to which the VI wrote data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.

1805893 #>.*2:
1806084 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1806263 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
1806354 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
1806588 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
1806724 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.

1814368 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1814547 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
1814675 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
1814898 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.

1920175 l7jac
1920365 Close File+.vi
1920459 *Reads a specified number of lines from a byte stream file beginning at a specified character offset.  The VI opens the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.
1920622 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1920842 number of lines is the maximum number of lines the VI reads.  The default value is -1 line, which means to read the entire file.  For this VI, a line is a character string ending with a carriage return, line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed; a string ending at the EOF; or a string that has the maximum line length specified by the max characters per line input.
1921224 start of read offset is the position in the file, measured in characters (or bytes), at which the VI begins reading.
1921342 max characters per line is the maximum number of characters the VI reads before ending the search for the end of a line.  The default is 0, which means that there is no limit to the number of characters the VI reads.
1921560 new file path is the path of the file from which the VI read data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
1921795 line string is the data read from the file.
1921840 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
1921980 EOF? is TRUE if you attempt to read past the end of file.
